### Comment by [@dejanzele](https://github.com/dejanzele) — 2023-12-07T20:01:22Z

How will you handle if a worker cluster fails for some reason (network issues, cluster goes down...)? Will you have some sort of job leases and job periodically reporting back they are still executing?

### Comment by [@dejanzele](https://github.com/dejanzele) — 2023-12-08T14:30:42Z

Will this KEP be focused only on `batch/v1 Job` resource or will it support some other CRDs also?

Will there be any issues with etcd if we are distributing let's say 10,000,000 jobs across N clusters, because as far as I understand the feature, you submit the resource to the management cluster which is then delegated to some worker cluster.

In cases of extreme load, will it cause issues with etcd?

For that reason we don't save the resources in etcd in the management cluster in Armada instead we save them into a DB. Also, I think it is possible to have fairly large job/pod definitions (up to ~100kb), so in case of extreme workload count, this can require a lot of storage.

### Comment by [@wenjiaswe](https://github.com/wenjiaswe) — 2023-12-09T03:03:42Z

> Will this KEP be focused only on `batch/v1 Job` resource or will it support some other CRDs also?
> 
> Will there be any issues with etcd if we are distributing let's say 10,000,000 jobs across N clusters, because as far as I understand the feature, you submit the resource to the management cluster which is then delegated to some worker cluster.
> 
> In cases of extreme load, will it cause issues with etcd?
> 
> For that reason we don't save the resources in etcd in the management cluster in Armada instead we save them into a DB. Also, I think it is possible to have fairly large job/pod definitions (up to ~100kb), so in case of extreme workload count, this can require a lot of storage.

cc @siyuanfoundation @serathius

### Comment by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-10T00:31:55Z

@dejanzele While the KEP focuses on the Job, the very same mechanisms will be applicable to all Kueue's integrations (Jobset, MPIJob, TFJob, RayJob, etc).

Yes, I guess there will be issues if you try to put 10 M jobs a day on the management cluster and try to distribute them across N clusters.  Not only connected to Etcd. 10 M/day is 115 jobs / sec on average, and each of them would require couple writes, emit some events etc. With, say, 10 writes per job we  would be at 1150 writes/s. Quite a lot. And there will be spikes. 

The jobs are supposed to do something. Getting images and starting pods for 115 jobs/s will put a significant burden on the worker clusters, and thats out of MultiKueue control. 

Sure, we could use something other than Etcd (Redis?) and also provide a dedicated API and tooling to submit jobs to the cluster (instead of creating them in Etcd). But then we will have troubles with user adoption and higher maintenance and development costs.

As the code doesn't exist yet in full, no tests were made so all scalability estimates are just handwaving, but the thing should hopefully work ok-ish up too ~1M/jobs per day (maybe more). If you need much more, you can create multiple separate MultiKueue environments.

### Comment by [@dejanzele](https://github.com/dejanzele) — 2023-12-11T00:15:55Z

@mwielgus
I agree fully with your response, makes sense.
Reason why I asked for this extreme load is that is is quite normal with Armada to schedule between 5-7 million Jobs per day and to have a peak throughput of around 8k Jobs/minute (which is around ~130 Jobs per second).

There are a lot of optimisation that can be applied like leveraging Dragonfly, cache databases, messaging systems... but that makes the final solution more complicated, moves away from k8s-native, and like you said, maintenance & development cost...

I really like this proposal, and you took a really interesting approach. I am definitely following this and eager to try it out :)

### Comment by [@Sharpz7](https://github.com/Sharpz7) — 2023-12-11T16:36:10Z

It would be great to see scheduling be bring-your-own, like it is with kube-scheduler. Is that possible?

### Comment by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-12-11T16:38:36Z

Can you expand? There is only one kube-scheduler. The rest are forks. And components in k8s can be replaced depending on your provider.

### Comment by [@Sharpz7](https://github.com/Sharpz7) — 2023-12-12T13:27:19Z

> Can you expand? There is only one kube-scheduler. The rest are forks. And components in k8s can be replaced depending on your provider.

@alculquicondor 
Basically, just an easier way to add custom "scheduling" logic for Kueue Jobs on the multi-cluster level. Sorry for the confusion, "scheduling" is a wider term in HPC. How do I define the difference between Scheduling of Pods, and "Scheduling" of Jobs by Kueue?

### Comment by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-12-12T15:24:17Z

So you are asking for the equivalent of the "kube-scheduler framework". IMO, that's a separate effort from Multi-cluster support. The canonical issue for that is https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/issues/10, but didn't make any progress. I still think we should focus on finishing core functionality before committing to the maintenance of a somewhat stable interface.

Also, one problem that I find with kube-scheduler framework is the proliferation of forks and reduction on contributions to the kube-scheduler.

### Comment by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2023-12-28T21:34:15Z

> @mwielgus Can a management cluster serve concurrently in the role of a worker cluster? We can imagine the following situation:
> 
> cluster A: Management And Worker cluster cluster B: Worker cluster

@mwielgus I'm waiting only for this.
If I miss any mentioning, please let me know.

### Comment by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-28T21:38:22Z

@tenzen-y Yes, such configuration will be possible in the future, once we establish https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/pull/4370 as a universal standard for selectively disabling controllers for other API/CRD objects.  Right now the only option for CRDs in the management cluster is to install API definitions but without controllers, that prevents allowing two roles inside one cluster.

### Comment by [@tenzen-y](https://github.com/tenzen-y) — 2023-12-28T21:45:42Z

> @tenzen-y Yes, such configuration will be possible in the future, once we establish [kubernetes/enhancements#4370](https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/pull/4370) as a universal standard for disabling controllers for other APIs/CRDs. Right now the only option for CRDs in the management cluster is to install API definitions but without controllers, that prevents allowing two roles inside one cluster.

@mwielgus It makes sense. Can we mention that in `NonGoals`? I think that we can say that multiple roles inside one cluster without [kubernetes/enhancements#4370](https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/pull/4370) can not be supported.

### Comment by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-28T21:50:55Z

+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueu) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them.
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point though which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
```

  Maybe we could use the image for the role-sharing scenario which seems to be the final goal?

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:73** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2023-11-29T12:34:22Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,216 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueu) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them.
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point though which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters (or they will be disabled). 
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker clusters. Deletion/suspension of the job 
```

  ```suggestion
  it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
  ```
  Can a job exist on multiple worker clusters?

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:192** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2023-11-29T12:36:10Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,216 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)

+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueu) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them.
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point though which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters (or they will be disabled). 
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker clusters. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigName string `json:"kubeconfigName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigLocation string `json:"kubeconfigLocation"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    KubeconfigLocationType LocationType `json:"kubeconfigLocationType"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueClusterStatus {
+   Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type"`
+}
+```
+
+MultiKueue controller will monitor all cluster definitions and maintain 
+the Kube clients for all of them. Any connectivity problems will be reported both in
+MultiKueuCluster status as well as AdmissionCheckStatus and Events. MultiKueue controller 
+will make sure that whenever the kubeconfig is refreshed, the appropriate 
+clients will also be recreated.
+
+Creation of kubeconfig files is outside of the MultiKueue scope, and is cloud
```

  Maybe we can state it in non-goals?

- **keps/693-multikueue/kep.yaml:14** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2023-11-29T12:37:36Z

+approvers:
+  - "@alculquicondor"
+
+# The target maturity stage in the current dev cycle for this KEP.
+stage: alfa
```

  ```suggestion
  stage: alpha
  ```

```

  I would like to see more explanation of what "disabled" means. I think the goal is to support role-sharing, in this case, we should have a way to disable per Job. For this purpose we need some standard label, or another mechanism for disabling. 
  
  If we state the need clearly here, I could maybe use it as reference in the design doc / KEP for its support in Job.

+default controller (or none at all)

+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.

+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`

+}

+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`

+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigName string `json:"kubeconfigName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigLocation string `json:"kubeconfigLocation"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    KubeconfigLocationType LocationType `json:"kubeconfigLocationType"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueClusterStatus {
+   Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type"`
+}
+```
+
+MultiKueue controller will monitor all cluster definitions and maintain 
+the Kube clients for all of them. Any connectivity problems will be reported both in
+MultiKueuCluster status as well as AdmissionCheckStatus and Events. MultiKueue controller 
+will make sure that whenever the kubeconfig is refreshed, the appropriate 
+clients will also be recreated.
+
+Creation of kubeconfig files is outside of the MultiKueue scope, and is cloud
```

  Added.

### Review by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) (commented) — 2023-11-29T14:08:41Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:67** by [@mimowo](https://github.com/mimowo) — 2023-11-29T14:08:41Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,220 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs.
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
```

  WDYT about the `leader` for the name, instead of the management cluster? Leader is used in the WIP PR https://github.com/kubernetes-sigs/kueue/pull/1360, and I like this name, but no strong opinion, it would be just good to align the vocab between the KEP and the implementation.

```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,216 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueu) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them.
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point though which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters (or they will be disabled). 
```

  Added.

+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are

+## Proposal

+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API.

+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")

+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)

+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.

+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller

+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.

+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:110** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-11-30T21:28:49Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,225 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
```

  ```suggestion
  MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
  ```

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:138** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-11-30T21:30:53Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,225 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)

+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)

+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
```

  If this is not expected to have an "status", then you can directly put the list here.

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:149** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-11-30T21:31:55Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,225 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigName string `json:"kubeconfigName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigLocation string `json:"kubeconfigLocation"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    KubeconfigLocationType LocationType `json:"kubeconfigLocationType"`
```

  if all these fields refer to "kubeconfig", they should probably be inside a single kubeconfig struct.

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:192** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-11-30T21:34:17Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,225 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigName string `json:"kubeconfigName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigLocation string `json:"kubeconfigLocation"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    KubeconfigLocationType LocationType `json:"kubeconfigLocationType"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueClusterStatus {
+   Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type"`
+}
+```
+
+MultiKueue controller will monitor all cluster definitions and maintain 
+the Kube clients for all of them. Any connectivity problems will be reported both in
+MultiKueuCluster status as well as AdmissionCheckStatus and Events. MultiKueue controller 
+will make sure that whenever the kubeconfig is refreshed, the appropriate 
+clients will also be recreated.
+
+Creation of kubeconfig files is outside of the MultiKueue scope, and is cloud
+provider/environment dependant.
+
+MultiKueue controller, when pushing workloads to the worker clusters, will use the same 
+namespace and local queue names as were used in the management cluster. It is user's 
+responsibility to set up the appropriate namespaces and local queues.
+Worker ClusterQueue definitions may be different than in the management cluster. For example,
+quota settings may be specific to the given location. And/or cluster queue may have different
+admission checks, use ProvisioningRequest, etc.
+
+When distributing the workloads across clusters MultiKueue controller will first create
+the Kueue's internal Workload object. Only after the workload is admitted and other clusters
+are cleaned-up the real job will be created, to match the Workload. That gives the guarantee
+that the workload will not start in more than one cluster.
+
+When the job is running MultiKueue controller will copy its status from worker cluster
+to the management cluster, to keep the impression that the job is running in the management 
+cluster. This is needed to allow pipelines and workflow engines to execute against 
+the management cluster with MultiKueue without any extra changes. 
+
+### Test Plan
+[x] I/we understand the owners of the involved components may require updates to
+existing tests to make this code solid enough prior to committing the changes necessary
+to implement this enhancement.
+
+#### Unit Tests
+The code will adhere to regular best practices for unit tests and coverage. 
+
+#### Integration tests
+Integration tests will be executed against a mocked client that will provide predefined
```

  ```suggestion
  Integration tests will be executed against mocked clients for the worker clusters that will provide predefined
  ```

+## Summary

+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.

+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
```

+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
```

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:110** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-05T11:39:50Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,225 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
```

  Done.

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-12-05T11:46:32Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:138** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-05T11:46:32Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,225 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
```

  I'm following the pattern from ProvisioningRequestConfig.

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-12-05T11:49:27Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:149** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-05T11:49:27Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,225 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the 
+startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigName string `json:"kubeconfigName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    KubeconfigLocation string `json:"kubeconfigLocation"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    KubeconfigLocationType LocationType `json:"kubeconfigLocationType"`
```

  Done.

+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.

+while maintaining the specified quota limits.

+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.

+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are 
+either location-flexible or are copying the data as a part of the

+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the

+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.

+

+

+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok),

+until some Kueue running there admits the workload.

+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.

+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. Noone will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller.

+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever

+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)

+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusig the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
