+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
```

  Could you have clusters that (themselves) are more ephemeral, and they are brought up when needed? This is the on-demand use case, but we don't have a persistent cluster bringing up on demand resources, we have more on-demand clusters.

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:167** by [@vsoch](https://github.com/vsoch) — 2023-12-13T17:29:08Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,234 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Information how to connect to the cluster.
+    KubeConfig KubeConfig `json:"kubeConfig"`
```

  Can we use leader -> follower instead of master / worker? Or leader/worker, main/worker? Not to be the politically correct bus driver, but I think the master and worker terms are not always looked well upon. :nerd_face:

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:211** by [@vsoch](https://github.com/vsoch) — 2023-12-13T17:31:55Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,234 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Information how to connect to the cluster.
+    KubeConfig KubeConfig `json:"kubeConfig"`
+}
+
+type KubeConfig struct {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    Name string `json:"configName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    Location string `json:"location"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    LocationType LocationType `json:"locationType"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueClusterStatus {
+   Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type"`
+}
+```
+
+MultiKueue controller will monitor all cluster definitions and maintain 
+the Kube clients for all of them. Any connectivity problems will be reported both in
+MultiKueuCluster status as well as AdmissionCheckStatus and Events. MultiKueue controller 
+will make sure that whenever the kubeconfig is refreshed, the appropriate 
+clients will also be recreated.
+
+Creation of kubeconfig files is outside of the MultiKueue scope, and is cloud
+provider/environment dependant.
+
+MultiKueue controller, when pushing workloads to the worker clusters, will use the same 
+namespace and local queue names as were used in the management cluster. It is user's 
+responsibility to set up the appropriate namespaces and local queues.
+Worker ClusterQueue definitions may be different than in the management cluster. For example,
+quota settings may be specific to the given location. And/or cluster queue may have different
+admission checks, use ProvisioningRequest, etc.
+
+When distributing the workloads across clusters MultiKueue controller will first create
+the Kueue's internal Workload object. Only after the workload is admitted and other clusters
+are cleaned-up the real job will be created, to match the Workload. That gives the guarantee
+that the workload will not start in more than one cluster.
+
+When the job is running MultiKueue controller will copy its status from worker cluster
+to the management cluster, to keep the impression that the job is running in the management 
+cluster. This is needed to allow pipelines and workflow engines to execute against 
+the management cluster with MultiKueue without any extra changes. 
```

  Just a high level comment - you might want to glance at Federated slurm (which has a similar idea) but I'm not sure the usability was there (note - I have not tried this, just sharing what I read last night): https://groups.google.com/g/slurm-users/c/CAxx-UHVjkQ/m/x-p1NKhoAAAJ
  
  > They were meant to actually be federated, but it confused our users, so I broke the federation again (but left the rest of the setup in place). 
  
  some of the ideas seem similar, might make sense to learn from them (it's been around like 7 years I think) https://slurm.schedmd.com/federation.html#jobscheduling

```

  > * the user has multiple clusters deployed
  
  yes 
  
  > * kueue is installed on all of them
  
  yes
  
  > * they are understood by kueue by way of ResourceFlavors?
  
  no, resource flavors stay as is. They are understood as MultiKueue AdmissionCheck parameters. Quota on the management cluster level represents the global quota.
  
  > * what permissions are needed?
  
  To manage jobs (and other Job-like crds supported by Kueue0 and Kueue's workloads in external clusters.
  
  > And for now we are assuming that the multiple clusters might have heterogeneous resources, and this is understood and mapped to on the level of the ResourceFlavor?
  
  Clusters can have heterogenous resources and globally the quota is managed in the same way as on a standalone cluster.

+until some Kueue running there admits the workload.
+If a remote workload is admitted first, the job will be created 
+in the remote cluster with a `kueue.x-k8s.io/prebuilt-workload-name` label pointing to that clone.
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining worker clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-12-13T18:32:12Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:107** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-13T18:32:12Z

@@ -0,0 +1,236 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)

+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)

+<!-- /toc -->

+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.

+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue to distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will clone it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload.
+If a remote workload is admitted first, the job will be created 
+in the remote cluster with a `kueue.x-k8s.io/prebuilt-workload-name` label pointing to that clone.
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining worker clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
```

  Some other controller (or a user, manually) may add or remove clusters in Kueue's ClusterQueue configuration as they come and go.

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-12-13T18:34:19Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:167** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-13T18:34:19Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,234 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Information how to connect to the cluster.
+    KubeConfig KubeConfig `json:"kubeConfig"`
```

  In the KEP we use the term management cluster and worker clusters.

### Review by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) (commented) — 2023-12-13T18:34:48Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:211** by [@mwielgus](https://github.com/mwielgus) — 2023-12-13T18:34:47Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,234 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Information how to connect to the cluster.
+    KubeConfig KubeConfig `json:"kubeConfig"`
+}
+
+type KubeConfig struct {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    Name string `json:"configName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    Location string `json:"location"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    LocationType LocationType `json:"locationType"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueClusterStatus {
+   Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type"`
+}
+```
+
+MultiKueue controller will monitor all cluster definitions and maintain 
+the Kube clients for all of them. Any connectivity problems will be reported both in
+MultiKueuCluster status as well as AdmissionCheckStatus and Events. MultiKueue controller 
+will make sure that whenever the kubeconfig is refreshed, the appropriate 
+clients will also be recreated.
+
+Creation of kubeconfig files is outside of the MultiKueue scope, and is cloud
+provider/environment dependant.
+
+MultiKueue controller, when pushing workloads to the worker clusters, will use the same 
+namespace and local queue names as were used in the management cluster. It is user's 
+responsibility to set up the appropriate namespaces and local queues.
+Worker ClusterQueue definitions may be different than in the management cluster. For example,
+quota settings may be specific to the given location. And/or cluster queue may have different
+admission checks, use ProvisioningRequest, etc.
+
+When distributing the workloads across clusters MultiKueue controller will first create
+the Kueue's internal Workload object. Only after the workload is admitted and other clusters
+are cleaned-up the real job will be created, to match the Workload. That gives the guarantee
+that the workload will not start in more than one cluster.
+
+When the job is running MultiKueue controller will copy its status from worker cluster
+to the management cluster, to keep the impression that the job is running in the management 
+cluster. This is needed to allow pipelines and workflow engines to execute against 
+the management cluster with MultiKueue without any extra changes. 
```

  Thank you for the pointer, will take a look.

  On a worker clusters you can have globaly shared ClusterQueue, that gets jobs from the management cluster but without GPUS and without borrowing allowed, and a local-only ClusterQueue with GPUS, in a single Cohort. Inside of a single ClusterQueue we don't differentiate workloads by their origin.

@@ -0,0 +1,240 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)

+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)

+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->

+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.

+until some Kueue running there admits the workload.

+in the remote cluster with a `kueue.x-k8s.io/prebuilt-workload-name` label pointing to that clone.
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining worker clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in

+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all).
+
+* Etcd may not provide enough performance (writes/s) to handle very large 
```

  nit: etcd should always be lower case ^_^

### Review by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) (commented) — 2023-12-14T18:26:29Z

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:67** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-12-14T18:12:58Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,234 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
```

  Can you summarize the ideas around "single point of failure" under risks and mitigations?

+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok),

+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
```

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:107** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-12-14T18:17:43Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,236 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue to distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will clone it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload.
+If a remote workload is admitted first, the job will be created 
+in the remote cluster with a `kueue.x-k8s.io/prebuilt-workload-name` label pointing to that clone.
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining worker clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
```

  worth adding as a note and/or non-goal

+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of

+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading

+

+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will clone it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload.
+If a remote workload is admitted first, the job will be created 
+in the remote cluster with a `kueue.x-k8s.io/prebuilt-workload-name` label pointing to that clone.
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining worker clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all).

+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest

+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all).

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:147** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-12-14T18:20:36Z

+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
```

  I think these can all be follow ups. Maybe mention in the "Alternatives" section?

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:175** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-12-14T18:21:48Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,234 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)
+  - [Risks and Mitigations](#risks-and-mitigations)
+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Information how to connect to the cluster.
+    KubeConfig KubeConfig `json:"kubeConfig"`
+}
+
+type KubeConfig struct {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    Name string `json:"configName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    Location string `json:"location"`
```

  Can you add a note that the namespace will be fixed to the namespace where kueue is running?

- **keps/693-multikueue/README.md:202** by [@alculquicondor](https://github.com/alculquicondor) — 2023-12-14T18:22:39Z
```diff
@@ -0,0 +1,234 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
+  - [Non-Goals](#non-goals)
+- [Proposal](#proposal)
+  - [User Stories (Optional)](#user-stories-optional)
+    - [Story 1](#story-1)
+    - [Story 2](#story-2)

+- [Design Details](#design-details)
+  - [Test Plan](#test-plan)
+    - [Unit Tests](#unit-tests)
+    - [Integration tests](#integration-tests)
+  - [Graduation Criteria](#graduation-criteria)
+- [Implementation History](#implementation-history)
+- [Drawbacks](#drawbacks)
+- [Alternatives](#alternatives)
+<!-- /toc -->
+
+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.
+
+## Motivation
+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of
+them utilized. Without a global distribution point, some clusters may
+get less jobs they are able to process, while the others get more, leading
+to underutilization and higher costs. 
+
+### Goals
+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.
+* Allow to upgrade single cluster Kueue deployments to multicluster without
+much hassle.
+
+### Non-Goals
+* Solve storage problem. It is assumed that the distributed jobs are
+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the 
+data as a part of the startup process.
+* Synchronize configuration across the clusters. It is expected that the 
+user will create the appropriate objects, roles and permissions
+in the clusters (manually, using gitops or some 3rd-party tooling).
+* Set up authentication between clusters.
+
+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Information how to connect to the cluster.
+    KubeConfig KubeConfig `json:"kubeConfig"`
+}
+
+type KubeConfig struct {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    Name string `json:"configName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    Location string `json:"location"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    LocationType LocationType `json:"locationType"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueClusterStatus {
+   Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type"`
+}
+```
+
+MultiKueue controller will monitor all cluster definitions and maintain 
+the Kube clients for all of them. Any connectivity problems will be reported both in
+MultiKueuCluster status as well as AdmissionCheckStatus and Events. MultiKueue controller 
+will make sure that whenever the kubeconfig is refreshed, the appropriate 
+clients will also be recreated.
+
+Creation of kubeconfig files is outside of the MultiKueue scope, and is cloud
+provider/environment dependant.
+
+MultiKueue controller, when pushing workloads to the worker clusters, will use the same 
+namespace and local queue names as were used in the management cluster. It is user's 
+responsibility to set up the appropriate namespaces and local queues.
+Worker ClusterQueue definitions may be different than in the management cluster. For example,
+quota settings may be specific to the given location. And/or cluster queue may have different
+admission checks, use ProvisioningRequest, etc.
+
+When distributing the workloads across clusters MultiKueue controller will first create
```

  With this design of MK, any improvements to the fair-share model will directly apply to MK. Resolving for now.

+# KEP-693: MultiKueue

+## Summary
+Introduce an new AdmissionCheck (called MultiKueue) with dedicated API
+and controller that will provide multi-cluster capabilities to Kueue.

+Many of Kueue's users are running multiple clusters and would like to
+have a way to easily distribute batch jobs across them to keep all of

+to underutilization and higher costs.

+* Allow Kueue distribute batch jobs across multiple clusters,
+while maintaining the specified quota limits.
+* Provide users with a single entry point through which the jobs
+can be submitted and monitored, just like they were running in
+a single cluster.
+* Be compatible with all Kueue's features (priorities, borrowing, preemptions, etc)
+and most of integrations.

+either location-flexible (for a subset of clusters) or are copying the

+## Proposal
+
+Introduce MultiKueue AdmissionCheck, controller and configuration API. 
+
+Establish the need for a designated management cluster.
+
+![Architecture](arch.png "Architecture")
+
+For each workload coming to a ClusterQueue (with the MultiKueue AdmissonCheck enabled)
+in the management cluster, and getting past the preadmission phase in the 
+two-phase admission process (meaning that the global quota is ok), 
+MultiKueue controller will create it in the defined worker clusters and wait 
+until some Kueue running there admits the workload. 
+Then it will remove the workloads from the remaining clusters and allow the
+single instance of the job to proceed. The workload will be also admitted in 
+the management cluster.
+
+There will be no job controllers running in the management clusters or they will be
+disabled for the workloads coming to MultiKueue-enabled cluster queues via annotation
+or some other, yet to be decided, mechanism. By disabling we mean that the controller
+will do no action on the selected objects, no pods (or other objects created and 
+allowing other controllets to update their status as they see fit.
+
+There will be just CRD/job definitions deployed. MultiKueue controller will copy the status
+of the job from the worker clusters, so that it will appear that the job
+is running inside the management clusters. However, as there is no job controller,
+no pods will be created in the management cluster. No controller will also overwrite
+the status that will be copied by the MultiKueue controller. 
+
+If the job, for whatever reason, is suspended or deleted in the management cluster,
+it will be deleted from the worker cluster. Deletion/suspension of the job 
+only in worker cluster will trigger the global job requeuing.
+Once the job finishes in the worker cluster, the job will also 
+finish in the management cluster.
+
+### User Stories (Optional)
+
+#### Story 1
+As a Kueue user I have clusters on different cloud providers and on-prem. 
+I would like to run computation-heavy jobs across all of them, wherever 
+I have free resources.
+ 
+#### Story 2
+As a Kueue user I have clusters in multiple regions of the same cloud 
+provider. I would like to run workloads that require the newest GPUs,
+whose on-demand availability is very volatile. The GPUs are available
+at random times at random regions. I want to use ProvisioningRequest
+to try to catch them.
+
+### Risks and Mitigations
+* Disabling the Job controller for all (or selected objects) may be problematic
+on environments where access to the master configuration is limited (like GKE).
+We are in talks with SIG-Apps to establish an acceptable way of using a non
+default controller (or none at all)
+
+## Design Details
+MultiKueue will be enabled on a cluster queue using the admission check fields.
+Just like ProvisioningRequest, MultiKueue will have its own configuration, 
+MultiKueueConfig with the following definition. To allow reusing the same clusters
+across many Kueues, additional object, MultiKueueWorkerCluster, is added.
+
+```go
+type MultiKueueConfig struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueConfigSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueConfigSpec struct {
+     // List of MultiKueueWorkerClusters names where the 
+     // workloads from the ClusterQueue should be distributed.
+     Clusters []string `json:"clusters,omitempty"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueCluster struct {
+    metav1.TypeMeta   `json:",inline"`
+    metav1.ObjectMeta `json:"metadata,omitempty"`
+    Spec MultiKueueClusterSpec `json:"spec,omitempty"`
+    Status MultiKueueClusterStatus `json:"status,omitempty"`
+}
+
+const (
+    // Location is the path on the disk.
+    PathLocationType LocationType = "Path"
+    
+    // Location is the name of the secret inside kueue-system namespace.
+    SecretLocationType LocationType = "Secret"
+)
+
+type MultiKueueuClusterSpec {
+    // Information how to connect to the cluster.
+    KubeConfig KubeConfig `json:"kubeConfig"`
+}
+
+type KubeConfig struct {
+    // Name of the custer inside the given KubeConfig.
+    Name string `json:"configName"`
+    
+    // Location of the KubeConfig.
+    Location string `json:"location"`
+    
+    // Type of the KubeConfig location.
+    LocationType LocationType `json:"locationType"`
+}
+
+type MultiKueueClusterStatus {
+   Conditions []metav1.Condition `json:"conditions,omitempty" patchStrategy:"merge" patchMergeKey:"type"`
+}
+```
+
+MultiKueue controller will monitor all cluster definitions and maintain 
+the Kube clients for all of them. Any connectivity problems will be reported both in
+MultiKueuCluster status as well as AdmissionCheckStatus and Events. MultiKueue controller 
+will make sure that whenever the kubeconfig is refreshed, the appropriate 
+clients will also be recreated.
+
+Creation of kubeconfig files is outside of the MultiKueue scope, and is cloud
+provider/environment dependant.
+
+MultiKueue controller, when pushing workloads to the worker clusters, will use the same 
+namespace and local queue names as were used in the management cluster. It is user's 
+responsibility to set up the appropriate namespaces and local queues.
+Worker ClusterQueue definitions may be different than in the management cluster. For example,
+quota settings may be specific to the given location. And/or cluster queue may have different
+admission checks, use ProvisioningRequest, etc.
+
+When distributing the workloads across clusters MultiKueue controller will first create
+the Kueue's internal Workload object. Only after the workload is admitted and other clusters
+are cleaned-up the real job will be created, to match the Workload. That gives the guarantee
+that the workload will not start in more than one cluster.
+
+When the job is running MultiKueue controller will copy its status from worker cluster
+to the management cluster, to keep the impression that the job is running in the management 
+cluster. This is needed to allow pipelines and workflow engines to execute against 
+the management cluster with MultiKueue without any extra changes. 
```

  It actually looks like a similar model already.

@@ -0,0 +1,240 @@
+# KEP-693: MultiKueue
+
+<!-- toc -->
+- [Summary](#summary)
+- [Motivation](#motivation)
+  - [Goals](#goals)
